References: <006d01c05a4d$c7ae3b80$59f6fbce@local> <20001130084019.G6233@hagbard.davep.org> <001b01c05b35$33c5a8c0$8604d2cc@san.rr.com>
Message-ID: <20001201075219.E6233@hagbard.davep.org>

On Thu, Nov 30, 2000 at 05:22:42PM -0800, Brian Hays wrote:
> Dave:
> > > Perhaps the HARBOUR_STRICT_CLIPPER_COMPATIBILITY flag should control
> > > this? If set, Directory() should force to upper before returning?
> >
> > I thought that HARBOUR_STRICT_CLIPPER_COMPATIBILITY was something that
> > "happened" at the time of building harbour itself? That doesn't sound
> > very useful.
> 
> I would agree that it is the least flexible solution, but it's probably
> true that if someone wants to build Harbour with
> HARBOUR_STRICT_CLIPPER_COMPATIBILITY these functions should return
> uppercase by default, agreed ??

Ahh, good question. I'm not sure about that. I'm tempted to say yes. 

> Would it make sense for anyone creating a Linux app to want
> HARBOUR_STRICT_CLIPPER_COMPATIBILITY ?

I can see a use for it, yes. Note that despite what has been reported it
isn't Linux that's different here, it's the possibility of encountering case
sensitive file systems (highly likely on a Linux (or Un*x) box but not a
given, case retentive and "everything's upper/lower" exist there too). If it
made sense for WinDos then it would make sense for Un*x.

Note, however, that for this to be useful the compatibility switched on my
that compile time switch would have to do a lot more than simply uppercase
filenames returned by directory() and friends (I'm sure this discussion has
been had before, in fact, I seem to recall it was used as the basis of a
previous grudge match <g>).

> I personally like harbour extensions via extra parameters, which give
> programmer options to call as desired or write wrappers or header files that
> default to personal standards.  I seem to remember some messages that
> discouraged this approach.
> But I would recommend an extra parameter to Directory and adir to control
> filename case. If passed, this would be the final answer.  If not, the SET
> setting proposed earlier would decide.

I think this is the wrong approach. Filename case is something that affects
many things and needs to be implemented at a lower level IMO. As I've said
many times before, FlagShip serves as a good example of a method of tackling
this problem.

--

#include "hbapi.h"
#include "hbapiitm.h"

#ifdef HB_EXTENSION

HB_FUNC( HB_PVALUE )
{
   USHORT uiParam =3D hb_parni( 1 );
   PHB_ITEM pBase =3D * hb_stack.pItems + ( * hb_stack.pBase =
)->item.asSymbol.stackbase; /* Skip function + self */

   if( uiParam && uiParam <=3D pBase->item.asSymbol.paramcnt ) /* Valid =
number */
      hb_itemReturn( pBase + 1 + uiParam );
}

#endif

Some applications run fine with the new stack files,
but some others sistematically GPF here:

hvm.c:

static void hb_vmPushStatic( USHORT uiStatic )
{
   PHB_ITEM pStatic;

   HB_TRACE(HB_TR_DEBUG, ("hb_vmPushStatic(%hu)", uiStatic));

>>> pStatic = s_aStatics.item.asArray.value->pItems + hb_stack.iStatics +
uiStatic - 1;
   if( HB_IS_BYREF( pStatic ) )
      hb_itemCopy( * hb_stack.pPos, hb_itemUnRef( pStatic ) );
   else
      hb_itemCopy( * hb_stack.pPos, pStatic );
   hb_stackPush();
}

Your help is really welcome! :-)

In-Reply-To: <3A27034F.A5D46C1C@user.rose.com>

** Reply to message from April <awhite@user.rose.com> on Thu, 30 Nov
2000 20:47:59 -0500

> > You'll find the answers to both of those questions at
> > http://www.mathematik.uni-bielefeld.de/~rainer/
> 
> I know I am trying your patience,

Not at all!

> but when the subj pages states:
> ...
> what is the difference?  is emx comparable (but not compatibile) to
> djgpp?

EMX is a Un*x emulation library for porting Un*x tools to DOS and OS/2.
RSXNT extends EMX support to 32-bit Windows (and DOS, using the 32-bit
DOS extender that is included with RSXNT). RSXNT has, in turn, been
ported to OS/2, in order to make it easier to write a single source that
targets all three platforms (DOS, OS/2, Windows).

RSXNTDJ is an add-on that allows people who are already using DJGPP to
create 32-bit DOS programs to also create 32-bit Windows programs
without having to switch to a totally new environment like RSXNT.

DJGPP is a DOS port of the Cygwin port of GCC, neither of which use the
EMX library.

So yes, EMX is comparable to DJGPP. Both provide a way to build Un*x
tools for non-Un*x platforms, using different means.
-- 
David G. Holm, Set Captain and all around
Harbour Project Clipper Compatibility fanatic.

Subject: [Harbour] 2000-12-03 15:05 UTC+0800 Ron Pinkas <ron@profit-master.com>

2000-12-03 15:05 UTC+0800 Ron Pinkas <ron@profit-master.com>
   * source/compiler/harbour.sly
     ! Optimized __GETA() support, and changed it to be implemented
identical to Clipper.
       /* Clipper passed a bGet Block which references the Base Array
Variable and not the Variable itself.
          Clipper passes NIL instead of bGet block if the Base Array is
MACROVAR or MACROTEXT.
          Clipper does not optimize "&Macro" to Macro, but Harbour does! */

   * source/rtl/tgetint.prg
     * __GETA() Changed 1st parameter aVar to bGetArray and logic to get the
Base Array if bGetArray is NIL
       /* Optimized to not use macro if possible (most cases) even if the
GetArray is a macro. */

   * tests/testget.prg
     + Added additional test.

Ryszard, this will require a small correction in hbexpra.c for Flex build.

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Mon Dec  4 04:15:04 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Martin Vogel)
Date: Mon Dec  4 04:15:04 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Multithreading
Message-ID: <000901c05dd3$2911f820$8ecbce81@martinvogel>

Harbourers,

although I have monitored this group, I am not aware of the current state
about the multithreading capability of Harbour. So please excuse any
redundant or non-finished thoughts in the following:

While implementing the HarbourToolsIII string functions, I have come across
the CSETREF() and other Set() functions. Straight forward programming, I
would have to add another comment stating
"/* TODO: make this thread safe */" when I am declaring the static/gobal
variables.

To make such static/global variables thread safe, one has to decide if the
variables ("stores")
should exist independantly in every thread (the WIN32 API calls that "Thread
Local Storage") or if they are shared by all threads (lets call that
"Process Global Storage").

So, to make it possible to write thread safe code - even if Harbour itself
is not MT ready - I suggest to add a hbthread module to the VM (or to the
RTL). The memory interface of this module could be like this:

<PSEUDOHEADER>

/* TLS functions */
PHB_MT_TLSTORE hb_mtTLSAlloc (int iMode);
int hb_mtTLSSetValue (PHB_MT_TLSTORE pStore, void *pValue);
void *hb_mtTLSGetValue (PHB_MT_TLSTORE pStore);
int hb_mtTLSFree (PHB_MT_TLSTORE pStore);
int hb_mtTLSGetMode (PHB_MT_TLSTORE pStore);

/* PGS functions */
PHB_MT_PGSTORE hb_mtPGSAlloc (int iMode);
void *hb_mtPGSReadLock (PHB_MT_PGSTORE pStore);
int hb_mtPGSReadUnlock (PHB_MT_PGSTORE pStore);
void *hb_mtPGSWriteLock (PHB_MT_PGSTORE pStore);
int hb_mtPGSSetValue (PHB_MT_PGSTORE pStore, void *pValue);
int hb_mtPGSWriteUnlock (PHB_MT_PGSTORE pStore);
int hb_mtPGSFree (PHB_MT_PGSTORE pStore);
int hb_mtPGSGetMode (PHB_MT_PGSTORE pStore);

</PSEUDOHADER>

hbthread would also be the place to implement the hb_createthread() and
other functions.

Using the above PGS functions in any module would look like this:

<PSEUDOCODE>

/* static siMode; */ /* should be a process wide variable */
static PHB_MT_PGSTORE spStore;

/* we need now a module init function that is executed at startup */
module_init_function()
{
   ...
   spStore =  hb_mtPGSAlloc (<ModesToDefine>);
   /* set initial value */
   hb_mtPGSSetValue (spStore, 0);
   ....
}

/* and an exit/cleanup function */
module_exit_function()
{
   ...
   hb_mitPGSFree (psStore);
   ...
}

...

/* function that uses (reads) the static var */
read_function()
{
  ...
  ...
  int iMode = hb_mtPGSReadLock (spStore);
    /* avoids that other threads change the content associated with this
slot */
  ...
  ...
  hb_mtPGSReadUnlock (spStore);
    /* don't call this before it is safe that other threads access (and
CHANGE) the content of this slot */
  ....
}

...

/* function that reads and CHANGES the static var */
read_and_write_function()
{
  ...
  ...
  int iMode = hb_mtPGSWriteLock (spStore);
    /* deny READ and write to other threads */
  ...

  hb_mtPGSSetValue (spStore, iMode+1);

  hb_mtPGSWriteUnlock (spStore);
    /* don't call this before it is safe that other threads access the
content of this slot */
  ....

}

</PSEUDOCODE>

The use of the TLS functions is very similar (altough we need some
mechanisms here to initialize
the variables when a new thread is started).

It is rather easy - so I think - to implement these functions transparently
for the single thread case, too. Once all module having static vars are
changed (remember: this has to be done anyway if we want to have MT),  this
would help to reduce ST/MT stuff to one source file.

Comments, questions please !

Regards

Martin



From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Mon Dec  4 04:45:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Ryszard Glab)
Date: Mon Dec  4 04:45:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Dynamic stack new files
In-Reply-To: <000001c05b68$a5c12980$0f2aa8c0@fivetechs>

On 1 Dec 2000, at 8:30, Antonio Linares wrote:

> But here are the first changed files. I really appreciate
> if some of you want to review my changes.

  IMHO, we should replace all (hb_stack.pBase + 1) with 
hb_stackFromBase(1) (or similar name) and (hb_stack.pPos - 1) with 
hb_stackFromTop(-1) to get clear access to the stack. These can be a 
function or a macro that will be easier to change in the future.

Regards, Ryszard

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Mon Dec  4 04:45:16 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Ryszard Glab)
Date: Mon Dec  4 04:45:16 2000
Subject: [Harbour] 2000-11-30 18:25 UTC+0800 Ron Pinkas <ron@profit-master.com>
In-Reply-To: <LOBBKAFMMFGJIKLMEPAKCEMEDHAA.ron@profit-master.com>

On 30 Nov 2000, at 18:31, Ron Pinkas wrote:

>    * source/compiler/harbour.y
>      * Added token GET (not used) just so that harboury.h is compatible with
> harbour.sly

  I don't think it is a good solution.

>    * source/rtl/tgetint.prg
>      * Reverted to use _1 and == NIL to not break Clipper compatibility.

  I would suggest a compromise solution:
IIF( PCOUNT()==0 .OR. HB_PVALUE(1)==NIL, cVar, cVar:=HB_PVALUE(1))
This will keep Clipper compatibility and will allow do edit database 
fields with '_1' name.
  Additionally maybe we need some runtime switch that will control the 
bahaviour of passing NIL to set/get codeblock. Simmilar situation is with 
MEMVARBLOCK() and FIELDBLOCK()

Regards, Ryszard

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Mon Dec  4 12:14:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Maurilio Longo)
Date: Mon Dec  4 12:14:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] CHANGELOG: 2000-12-04 17:54 GMT+1
Message-ID: <3A2BD0C0.BE9EB7CC@libero.it>

2000-12-04 17:54 GMT+1 Maurilio Longo <maurilio.longo@libero.it>
   * source/rtl/tbrowse.prg
     * I've rewritten from scratch stabilization and movement keys
handling.
       They were simply broken in previous TBrowse. They are now nearly
100% clipper compatible.
       DBU now works correctly when lastrec() + 1 is reached and leaved.
       ::stable state and ::HitTop or ::HitBottom were wrongly set
_before_ stabilization and not
       during as it should. ::GoBottom() was not calling
::goBottomBlock.
       Movement handling methods were calling ::skipBlock and they
should not, this was
       causing unneeded skipping being requested to data source.
       I hope these last changes have fixed TBrowse class. Please test
it extensively.

Luiz,

These were 2 simple bugs in TGet class, which I just fixed, and will upload
in few minutes.

You could also avoid the problem by replacing:

    oGet := GetNew()

with:

    oGet := GetNew( nRow++, nCol + 4, t(aChoices[nGet]), cVar )

And comment the :row, :col, :block and :name [later] assignments.

Ron

Hi Jean F.

TError.prg appear to be broken. Calling ErrorNew() now GPFs because it
causes some RT error and thus calls itself recursively.

Might it be related to your work in progress?

...Later,

The problem is in Method Instance() line 255 of TClass.prg:

   oInstance:Class := Self:Class

This line causes a RT Error, commenting this line circumvents this error!

Ron

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Tue Dec  5 08:40:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Patrick Mast)
Date: Tue Dec  5 08:40:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Need advice about C++ -> Harbour
In-Reply-To: <20001205125016.D6233@hagbard.davep.org>
Message-ID: <NCBBJKNMIDPJNLJCHCHIOEFKFKAA.harbour@winfakt.com>

Dave,

> > Is there a difference for name mangling for ANSI C code and C++ code?
> Yes, C++ does name mangling, C doesn't. Again, I'll mention the 
> Clipper FAQ entry 
> <URL:http://www.hagbard.demon.co.uk/clipper-faq/clipper-4.html#ss8.12>
> that deals with this very issue. It's probably as pertinent to 
> harbour as it is to CA-Clipper (unless harbour does that as part
> of it's harbour function declaration, but you need to check this
> so you know what your problem actually is).

Ok, so I need to do it like this?
,----------
| #ifdef __cplusplus
| extern "C" {
| #endif
| HB_FUNC ( IMGINIT )
| {
|  _ISInitialize("{xxxxxxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxxxxxxxxxx}");
| }
| #ifdef __cplusplus
| }
|#endif
`----------------------------

regards,

Patrick Mast
www.Patrick.Be.kz


From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Tue Dec  5 09:23:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Dave Pearson)
Date: Tue Dec  5 09:23:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Need advice about C++ -> Harbour
In-Reply-To: <NCBBJKNMIDPJNLJCHCHIOEFKFKAA.harbour@winfakt.com>; from harbour@winfakt.com on Tue, Dec 05, 2000 at 02:39:43PM +0100
References: <20001205125016.D6233@hagbard.davep.org> <NCBBJKNMIDPJNLJCHCHIOEFKFKAA.harbour@winfakt.com>
Message-ID: <20001205142150.I6233@hagbard.davep.org>

On Tue, Dec 05, 2000 at 02:39:43PM +0100, Patrick Mast wrote:
> Dave,
> 
> Ok, so I need to do it like this?
> ,----------
> | #ifdef __cplusplus
> | extern "C" {
> | #endif
> | HB_FUNC ( IMGINIT )
> | {
> |  _ISInitialize("{xxxxxxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxxxxxxxxxx}");
> | }
> | #ifdef __cplusplus
> | }
> |#endif
> `----------------------------

I don't think you want to wrap all of the code with that. Here's a little
experiment I've just done on your behalf. Note that this is with GCC on a
GNU/Linux box but the principles should be the same no matter.

Right, I've got a function written in C++ (note, not C, C++):

,----
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ cat foo.cc
| #include <hbapiitm.h>
| 
| HB_FUNC( FOO )
| {
|     hb_retc( "Hello, World" );
| }
`----

I compile it using a C++ compiler and then inspect the names within the
object file:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ g++ -c foo.cc -I${HB_INC_INSTALL}
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ nm foo.o
| 00000000 T HB_FUN_FOO__Fv
| 00000000 ? __FRAME_BEGIN__
| 00000000 t gcc2_compiled.
|          U hb_retc
`----

Note that HB_FUN_FOO doesn't exist as a function name but there is a mangled
name HB_FUN_FOO__Fv.

Ok, now I prefix the function declaration with the "don't mangle"
incantation:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ cat foo.cc
| #include <hbapiitm.h>
| 
| extern "C" HB_FUNC( FOO )
| {
|     hb_retc( "Hello, World" );
| }
`----

and compile and inspect again:

,----
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ g++ -c foo.cc -I${HB_INC_INSTALL}
| davep@hagbard:~/temp$ nm foo.o
| 00000000 T HB_FUN_FOO
| 00000000 ? __FRAME_BEGIN__
| 00000000 t gcc2_compiled.
|          U hb_retc
`----

notice that the name isn't mangled this time?

So, working on the results of that experiment I'd start by writing your code
as:

,----
| extern "C" HB_FUNC( IMGINIT )
| {
|     _ISInitialize("{xxxxxxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxxxxxxxxxx}");
| }
`----

and play on from there.

-- 
The Harbour Project: A free software Clipper compatible compiler
Home Page..........: http://www.harbour-project.org/
FAQ................: http://www.harbour-project.org/faq/harbour.html
My harbour page....: http://www.hagbard.demon.co.uk/harbour/

Martin,
            I wish you luck in accomplishing such a task as making Harbour
Thread-Safe. My personal impression is that, due to the fact that this was
NOT an issue when first brought up, Harbour is today as far from TS as from
Mars. Almost ALL the state of the executing program is based on
static/global values. There is no "Environment" where an instruction pointer
advances with it's stack and rest of stuff. Are you aware of this?

Regards
Harrier

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Tue Dec  5 10:16:01 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Martin Vogel)
Date: Tue Dec  5 10:16:01 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Multithreading
References: <3A2CFCCE.6747C3AA@urz.uni-heidelberg.de> <001b01c05ed3$3e729160$456410ac@jharrier>
Message-ID: <3A2D06C0.79EADC56@urz.uni-heidelberg.de>

Harrier,

many thanks for your wishes.

I am totally aware of the fact that making harbour thread-safe will be very much and hard work - 
that I cannot manage alone. But I think it is common sense that making harbour thread safe is
valuable
the effort, isn't it ?

So, it was my plan to implement first a transparent API to manage thread local storages, semaphores, 
etc... That done, we can go on - step by step - and replace the static / global data. When it comes
to
things like symbol table, vm stack, etc.. I will need the help of you guys - that's for sure - so be
prepared <g>.

Since the xBase language can be made multithreaded (proof by example <g>), Harbour can be made MT ! 

Regards

Martin

John, Brian,

don't worry. I will not upload any MT-code to the CVS tree that will
destabilize Harbour (
I haven't write acces anyway and don't need it at the moment.)

Let's simply see how far I get with some initial code and then we can see
where we can create a "meeting point" for the MT people. Since I suspect
that many module have to be changed, a second tree would be a solution where
we don't disturb the development of "Harbour v1.0". OTOH, we have then to
take more care to keep other, non-MT changes synchronized in both trees.

We don't have to decide that now, let's first collect some experiences.

Best regards

Martin

Subject: [Harbour] Eval stack changes
Message-ID: <3A2E8938.8976.485ACD2@localhost>

--Message-Boundary-26453
Content-type: text/plain; charset=US-ASCII
Content-transfer-encoding: 7BIT
Content-description: Mail message body

  I am attaching a draft for modifications of the eval stack code. There 
are two new files: estack.c and hbstack.h. These are the main files that 
handle the eval stack.
  There are new functions (or macros if HB_STACK_MACROS is defined) to 
access the stack. Using functions/macros instead of direct access should 
allow for easier future modifications (NIL pushing, multithread support, 
etc).

  This is not finished yet. If there will be an agreement for such 
changes then I can change it during this weekend and upload them into CVS 
repository.

Any comments? (Antonio?)

Regards, Ryszard

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Wed Dec  6 15:27:01 2000

Subject: [Harbour] Bug in Harbour Pre-Processor
Message-ID: <001e01c05fc2$c0f74aa0$08f4c4a1@gustavo>

I am testing harbour and find this bug in the pre-processor (well,comparated
with clipper).

//
// Test harbour 010.1
//
#xcommand Test( <Par1> [,<ParN>] ) => QQOut( <Par1> )[;QQOut(<ParN>)]
Test( Var1 ) // Line 1
Test( Var1, Var2 ) // Line 2
// eof

Run...

In clipper i have it:

QQOut( Var1 )
QQOut( Var1 );QQOut(Var2)

In harbour i have it:

Test(Var1 ) // <- Note
QQOut(Var1 );QQOut(Var2)
****
To fix it, i need to create a new command without the use of optional
parameters.

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Wed Dec  6 17:00:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Wed Dec  6 17:00:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] MemoLine bug
Message-ID: <000b01c05fcf$ae1562c0$8604d2cc@san.rr.com>

MemoLine is supposed to pad out lines to the line length (default 79).
But when it hits a blank line (two hard returns in a row) it returns an
empty string (should be 79 spaces).
Since an empty string is the "control" for reading past the end, this breaks
any implementation that loops through a file's contents.

MLTest.PRG:
#define CRLF Chr(13) +Chr(10)

FUNCTION Main ()
local i, cLine
local cStr := "abcdefg" + CRLF+ CRLF+ "AB"
local n := mlcount(cStr, 254)

FOR i := 1 TO n
   cLine := memoline(cStr, 254, i)
   ? len(cLine)
NEXT
?
RETURN (NIL)
// End Main

Output:
254
0                    <<< should be 254 !
254

Brian Hays
Abacus Data Systems, Inc



From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Wed Dec  6 19:30:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Wed Dec  6 19:30:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] CHANGELOG: 2000-12-06 16:09 UTC-0800  (For Alexander)
Message-ID: <000b01c05fe4$ba94ccb0$8604d2cc@san.rr.com>

I bear greetings and a present from Alexander!
He's deep in a project and hasn't been with us for a few weeks, but he found
time to make some small fixes to dbfntx!
It's not finished, but these do correct the relation between dbfntx and the
new super RDD

Remember, for dnfntx to work you need to add a line in the prg :
 rddRegister( "DBFNTX", 1 )
 or do something to force dbfntx0 be linked, as it was before (dbfcdx is
currently still set as the default driver).

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec  8 17:11:11 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Maurilio Longo)
Date: Fri Dec  8 17:11:11 2000
Subject: [Harbour] CHANGELOG: 2000-12-08 18:45 GMT+1
Message-ID: <3A31216C.F65666F5@libero.it>

2000-12-08 18:45 GMT+1 Maurilio Longo <maurilio.longo@libero.it>
   * source/rtl/tbrowse.prg
     ! I've fixed all known (to me) issues with latest TBrowse code.
       ::HitTop/Bottom were set back to .F. if a ::RefreshAll() was
issued. This is wrong since only
       movement keys can reset them.
       Issuing a long sequence of K_UP/K_DN (or CTRL_...) resulted on
wrong movement of datasource (you could
       even go backward using K_DN :-O)
       You could get an out of bounds moving around inside tbrowse.
     * Note that original Clipper TBrowse caches displayed rows, so
moving left or right does not require
       calling ::Skipblock to refresh screen. Present implementation of
TBrowse has not such a cache so
       a lot more of skipping around is needed.
-- 

 __________                   
|  |  | |__| md2520@mclink.it 
|_|_|_|____| Team OS/2 Italia

> handle the eval stack.

-----Mensaje original-----
De: harbour-admin@lists.harbour-project.org
[mailto:harbour-admin@lists.harbour-project.org]En nombre de Brian Hays
Enviado el: mircoles, 06 de diciembre de 2000 22:59
Para: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org
Asunto: [Harbour] MemoLine bug


MemoLine is supposed to pad out lines to the line length (default 79).
But when it hits a blank line (two hard returns in a row) it returns an
empty string (should be 79 spaces).
Since an empty string is the "control" for reading past the end, this breaks
any implementation that loops through a file's contents.

MLTest.PRG:
#define CRLF Chr(13) +Chr(10)

FUNCTION Main ()
local i, cLine
local cStr := "abcdefg" + CRLF+ CRLF+ "AB"
local n := mlcount(cStr, 254)

FOR i := 1 TO n
   cLine := memoline(cStr, 254, i)
   ? len(cLine)
NEXT
?
RETURN (NIL)
// End Main

Output:
254
0                    <<< should be 254 !
254

Brian Hays
Abacus Data Systems, Inc

Roberto,

"Microsoft think to make .NET multiplatform... and I think they'll
reach the goal."

The list of things MS have promised but not delivered over the last
(say) 10 years is huge.  This is especially true of their multi-/cross-
platform promises.  I'd wait until they deliver (if they do) before
committing any effort or plans to it!

Hmm... anyone using MS-DDE from UNIX/Linux to an app running on
Windows?  Using OLE in that way?  ActiveX controls?  DCOM?

They've even dropped support of most chips (MIPS etc) for NT/W2K!

Let's revisit this topic when/if MS get C# through the standardisation
process they've promised (promises are easy), and when/if .NET is
multi-platform in a meaningful way.  I guess a delay of 2-5 years at
least, and more likely 5-10 years (yes, really - I doubt very much
that they'll deliver what they've promised).  They've not even written
a proper specification for this stuff yet!!

John.

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Tue Dec 12 01:34:01 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Tue Dec 12 01:34:01 2000
Subject: [Harbour] macro expansion gpfs creating error object
Message-ID: <001101c06405$4ee41b40$8604d2cc@san.rr.com>

Ryszard & others:

I have a consistent gpf running this line of code:
   ? type("address")
-- or --
    cStr := "address"
    ? type(cStr)

This is in my large FWH app. I cannot duplicate it in a test applet
<<breaking news: yes I can, see below>>.

Basicallly I'm in a loop expanding expressions from a text file.  The
constant "address" is a special case that I handle, but after I test the
string with the Type() function.  If I remove that line, all is well, so
this isn't a random gpf.
The app goes into a loop and bombs with a tall stack of ErrorNew(65) and
TCLASS:INSTANCE() calls.
Apparently these two are in an infinite loop.
I do have a function called Address(), but without the parentheses this
should not be an issue and Type() should simply return "U" as it does in a
small test. There's no good reason why it would throw and error.

In writing this, I realized what to test. This little prg will gpf because
Type() is passed the name of a valid function. This really should return
"U":


function Main()
   ? "Use..."
   ? type("address")
return

FUNCTION address ()
RETURN (.t.)

Brian Hays
Abacus Data Systems, Inc

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Wed Dec 13 11:26:01 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Maurilio Longo)
Date: Wed Dec 13 11:26:01 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Multithreading
References: <003701c064e7$e36a6e80$0f2aa8c0@fivetechs> <3A37482A.2D871A4@urz.uni-heidelberg.de>
Message-ID: <3A37A2F8.B25B0355@libero.it>

Martin, Antonio,

am I wrong or do we need to protect only PUBLICs? 

Everything else can go to thread local memory (I mean thread stack)
since I simply use harbour pcode interpreter as thread function so it
simply starts and reinits all local variables and symbols. 
Public ones should be synchronized at the harbour language level, that
is:

nValue += 1

should be thread safe if nValue is a public variable.

In my opinion work areas should be local to threads.

regards.

PS. Maybe it is not so simple :-)

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Wed Dec 13 11:39:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Jesus Salas)
Date: Wed Dec 13 11:39:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Re: MultiThreading implementation
References: <NCBBJKNMIDPJNLJCHCHICELCFKAA.harbour@winfakt.com>
Message-ID: <002501c06522$fe0e5720$f801a8c0@clearcase.rd.com>

In the first months of life oh Harbour i was implementing the multithreading
model into its VM. ( for Windows version )

I think that i have the original code for multithreading at my home's
computer....

My modifications in Harbour VM was based on the System Stack access with
some defines that don't really modify so much the original code....

And some functions for control the threads runtime



If you want I can send the code that turn on to Multithread de VM of harbour

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Wed Dec 13 12:56:01 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Martin Vogel)
Date: Wed Dec 13 12:56:01 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Multithreading
References: <003701c064e7$e36a6e80$0f2aa8c0@fivetechs> <3A37482A.2D871A4@urz.uni-heidelberg.de> <3A37A2F8.B25B0355@libero.it>
Message-ID: <3A37B86F.47E71A72@urz.uni-heidelberg.de>

Maurilio,

> am I wrong or do we need to protect only PUBLICs?

That depends on what we decide should be thread local or "process global". 
But there are many problems. Think of code like this:

<PSEUDOCODE>
proc main

  private testprivate := 5
  ...
  CreateThread ("threadfunc", xParam)
  ...
return

func threadfunc (xParam)

  local testlocal := testprivate+1  // see below
  ...

return
</PSEUDOCODE>

As threadfunc is called by the main func, shouldn't it have access to a symbol named "testprivate" ?
Can we pass parameters to the threadfunction ? If we do, what about detached locals in a codeblock
passed as parameter ?
If we decide that only PUBLICs are process global, do we make a full copy of all privates in a
thread when this thread creates a new thread ?
Arrays are complex variable types, is it safe to code like this ?

<PSEUDOCODE>
func xyz
local aCopyOfMySettings
  ...
  public aMySettings := {.T., .F., 1, 0, 12, "A"}
  
  aCopyOfMySettings := aMySettings

  aCopyOfMySettings[1] := .F.  // access to data via local symbol -> dangerous if only public
symbols are protected
  ...

return
</PSEUDOCODE>

Don't get me wrong, these are just questions/possible problems. We can decide that code like that
above is allowed but very dangerous and no good coding style in MT mode. But I don't think that this
is a good solution...

> Everything else can go to thread local memory (I mean thread stack)
> since I simply use harbour pcode interpreter as thread function so it
> simply starts and reinits all local variables and symbols.
> Public ones should be synchronized at the harbour language level, that
> is:
> 
> nValue += 1
> 
> should be thread safe if nValue is a public variable.

See above.

> In my opinion work areas should be local to threads.

As a guideline I think that we should make as few restrictions as possible. I can think of some
cases where
"public" WAs can be very useful. The more the user can decide (and code) what he wants, the better.
It's even possible to implement MT without having major MT support on the HVM level (i.e. no
automatic data protection),
so that the user has to code everything himself (like on the C level). Not very comfortable, I know.

So we need to clarify what MT constructs / language elements we include on the Harbour language
level and how MT
works in Harbour (making copies of symbols and data, sharing WA or not or both,...)
That done, we rest is simple work <g>.

Your opinions ?

Martin

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Wed Dec 13 13:19:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Maurilio Longo)
Date: Wed Dec 13 13:19:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Multithreading
References: <003701c064e7$e36a6e80$0f2aa8c0@fivetechs> <3A37482A.2D871A4@urz.uni-heidelberg.de> <3A37A2F8.B25B0355@libero.it> <3A37B86F.47E71A72@urz.uni-heidelberg.de>
Message-ID: <3A37BD69.45F1B89F@libero.it>

Martin,

I think in your first example you can pass testprivate to your thread
(since thread procedures can receive an ULONG, at least on OS/2 and
win32).

And if you need to access more than one variable (like in your second
example) you can pass a pointer to a public array where you store
everything.

PUBLICs should be serialized at the hvm level. That is, VM needs to
acquire a semaphore before reading/writing to a public variables (and
PUBLIC arrays or objects as well).

In your second example, local variable aCopyOfMySettings is a local copy
of a public array, so if you change an element you change your local
copy, not the public one, if you want to change the public one, why do
you make a copy of it?

Local WAs give us a bonus (I think), you don't have to make them thread
safe, or else you need a semaphore somewhere which every method of a
given work area needs to acquire before doing anything. 

And, last thought, I don't want to have to handle semaphores myself,
that is I'd like to have MT support at the harbour language level.

regards.

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Thu Dec 14 07:48:01 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Martin Vogel)
Date: Thu Dec 14 07:48:01 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Multithreading
References: <003701c064e7$e36a6e80$0f2aa8c0@fivetechs> <3A37482A.2D871A4@urz.uni-heidelberg.de> <3A37A2F8.B25B0355@libero.it> <3A37B86F.47E71A72@urz.uni-heidelberg.de> <3A37BD69.45F1B89F@libero.it>
Message-ID: <3A38C18C.EA3D9027@urz.uni-heidelberg.de>

Maurilio,

> And if you need to access more than one variable (like in your second
> example) you can pass a pointer to a public array where you store
> everything.

It's not as easy IMO. Even if we let only the PUBLICs be process global, you could store
an array (see below) or a codeblock to it. This codeblock could have a detached local in it.
How to handle and synchronize access to this local variable ?

> PUBLICs should be serialized at the hvm level. That is, VM needs to
> acquire a semaphore before reading/writing to a public variables (and
> PUBLIC arrays or objects as well).

It is rather easy to synchronize the access to "simple" data types like integers or strings.
But there are problems with arrays, objects and codeblocks. That's why I said that we may need some
new language constructs (or even simpler, some synchronization functions) to handle such 
global data.

> In your second example, local variable aCopyOfMySettings is a local copy
> of a public array, so if you change an element you change your local

The last time I used Cli**er, aCopyOfMySettings, assigned to as
 
  aCopyOfMySettings := aMySettings

contained a copy of the _reference_ to the array, so changing the element aCopyOfMySettings[1]
would change aMySettings[1], too. Has this behaviour changed in Harbour ? 

> copy, not the public one, if you want to change the public one, why do
> you make a copy of it?

This was just an example that synchronizing the access to public symbols alone is not enough to make
a program really MT safe. One has to protect the _data_ and I think we have to find a consistent way
to do that
(at the HVM or Harbour language level).

> Local WAs give us a bonus (I think), you don't have to make them thread
> safe, or else you need a semaphore somewhere which every method of a
> given work area needs to acquire before doing anything.

Yes, local WAs are easier to handle than global ones (and are certainly faster). But there might be
situations where global WAs can be of good use. So I is my opinion that Harbour shouldn't restrict
WAs to local or global but let the user decide.

> And, last thought, I don't want to have to handle semaphores myself,
> that is I'd like to have MT support at the harbour language level.

That's ok. But to keep Harbour as open as possible we have to find a way that:

1. Those users who don't want to handle with MT stuff directly, get _automatic_ MT support by the
HVM for some
   very clearly defined situations. Further, this automatic MT support must not introduce critical
situations to the
   HVM itself (see my examples about arrays, codeblocks, ...). 

2. Create MT language elements for those user who want to handle MT stuff directly (e.g. sharing a
file handle for whatever reason)

I think that introducing an MT API on the HVM (that is C-) level is "rather easy". We need functions
to synchronize
access to resources, functions to start and stop threads, functions to access thread local data etc.
that work independant
from the MT library used (we may even think of a MT library for the single thread case to keep HVM
code changes small.)

But the other problem, how MT is introduced on the language level, is still unclear to me...
As you did, I also thought about making PUBLICs global and simply adding a semaphore object to each
PUBLIC symbol that
controls the access to the data associated with this symbol. But this may cause problems as I showed
above. We could say
that this is not our problem but the user's, that he has to copy or clone all public data before
using and changing them locally. Is this ok ? What do the others think ?

In principle, we could also solve this problem by adding a semaphore to each data element referenced
to by a public symbol. 
Or, in other words, we could provide the possibility to "mark" a certain data element as shared so
that the HVM uses
automatically a semaphore when accessing this data. But then, when do we mark this element ? When a
PUBLIC symbol is declared ? When data is assigned to a public ? What do we do when PUBLICs are
released and there are still other references to the data element so that it is not deleted ?

I'm not sure what the best solution is. What do you think ? 

Regards 

Martin

Dipl.-Phys. Martin Vogel

University of Heidelberg
Im Neuenheimer Feld 326
69120 Heidelberg
Tel.: +49 6221 54 4089

On 14 Dec 2000, at 13:37, Sid Saylors wrote:

> Error E2141 source\vm\estack.c 347: Declaration syntax error
> *** 1 errors in Compile ***

  Pleas, try to copy the following declaration from hvm.c into estack.c

#if defined(HB_INCLUDE_WINEXCHANDLER)
  #define HB_OS_WIN_32_USED
#endif

before any #include statement.

Regards, Ryszard

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Thu Dec 14 18:43:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Ron Pinkas)
Date: Thu Dec 14 18:43:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] New stack files (Ryszard)
In-Reply-To: <3A393D81.78B3E15A@home.com>
Message-ID: <LOBBKAFMMFGJIKLMEPAKOEBBDIAA.ron@profit-master.com>

Sid,

You probably have to fix your bcc configuration files! Here is what you need
in bcc5\bin\bcc32.cfg:

-I"c:\Bcc55\include"
-L"c:\Bcc55\lib;c:\Bcc55\lib\psdk"
-lj"c:\Bcc55\lib;c:\Bcc55\lib\psdk"

Please note the psdk portion.

And this in bcc55\bin\ilink32.cfg:

-L"c:\Bcc55\lib;c:\Borland\Bcc55\lib\psdk"

Ron

You are welcome to send me the two set of sample. Thanks,

PS: I don't forget the problem of ::CLass:... don't worry, I even had 
here some good result but where a bit stopped by the stack move.

My most important problem is to keep the compatibility with the 
actual implementation where the Class VAR are accessed directly 
(without the ::class sender)

One solution could be to keep the two kind of Class VARs, where 
CLASS DATA could stay as it (without ::Class sender) and CLASS 
VAR would work as with CLass(y). Regarding the CLASS 
METHOD as there is actually no implementation, I think we could 
access it by the ::class sender without any problem with the actual 
code.

Charles Kwon,

I'm a bit confused. It was my understanding that .NET is a kind of a new,
"Language Independent"*, alternative to MFC?

If so, and if someone wanted to have support for .NET in Harbour, wouldn't
it require research of the "Common Language Runtime" (CLR)?

I don't think this has anything to do with C#, nor Harbour Code Generation.

It seems that if someone found how to implement the (MS) CLR for Harbour,
then conceivably one could use the .NET framework as an alternative to using
FWH, and C4W for GUI.

While this will not be O/S independent (ALFN), it could be an interesting
feature.

*"Language Independent" = MSVB, MSVC++, C#, VBScript, JavaScipt, (any other
language that supports the MS CLR?).

Ron

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec 15 17:22:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Fri Dec 15 17:22:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] losing arrays
Message-ID: <000901c066e5$4462bf40$8604d2cc@san.rr.com>

My FWH app is having large arrays become NIL for no good reason.
I have multi-dim array "pseudo-objects" that store all the properties for
custom reports, screens and other items.
When the variable holding the array is passed by reference (yes, with "@"
because the called function may assign a new array altogether), down two
levels, a new array comes back up, but when it is then passed to another
function it is sometimes a NIL.

Could this be a garbage collection issue?

If I remove the "@" the problem goes away, but this of course creates
problems when a new array gets created below and assigned to that variable.

I have been unable to duplicate the problem with a small test prg.
But this is code that has worked in clipper and later FW for 5 years at
least, so it seems like a fairly critical issue. I can re-write my code to
get around it, but harbour really should handle it correctly.

Below is a test prg that illustrates the kinds of calls being made, but it
works fine.
Any ideas how to pursue this? In the app, the only thing between when it's
an array an when it's NIL is a FWH "wait state" with a dialog waiting for
input.  If I click any button and test the valtype, it is nil.
TIA
Brian Hays
Abacus Data Systems, Inc

function Main()

   local i, cStr, aTmp

   aTmp := array(20,10)
   aTmp[1,1] := 1
   aTmp[2,2] := 2

   func1(@aTmp)
   wait
   ? "Main1", valtype(aTmp)
   func2(aTmp)
   wait
   ? "Main2", valtype(aTmp)
   func3(@aTmp)
   wait
   ? "Main3", valtype(aTmp)

return nil

FUNCTION func1 (aTmp)
aTmp[1,1] := 11
? valtype(aTmp), aTmp[1,1], aTmp[2,2]
   func2(aTmp)
   ? "f1-2", valtype(aTmp)
   func3(@aTmp)
   ? "f1-3", valtype(aTmp)
RETURN (NIL)

FUNCTION func2 (aTmp)
aTmp := {{3,3},{4,4}}
? valtype(aTmp), aTmp[1,1], aTmp[2,2]
   wait
RETURN (NIL)

FUNCTION func3 (aTmp)
? valtype(aTmp), aTmp[1,1], aTmp[2,2]
   wait
RETURN (NIL)

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec 15 18:52:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Ron Pinkas)
Date: Fri Dec 15 18:52:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Visual Studio .NET Framework!!!!
In-Reply-To: <200012151314_MC2-BEBA-DF86@compuserve.com>
Message-ID: <LOBBKAFMMFGJIKLMEPAKEEBKDIAA.ron@profit-master.com>

John,

Just to clarify,

1. I am not an MS advocate.

2. The "Language Independent" was quoted and astericized exactly because I
don't necessarily agree with the description.

3. .NET It is pushed by MS as a Language Independent technology, because
from the architecture stand point, it is indeed language and even CPU
independent.

4. While MS currently offers 4 CLR compliant compilers, MS claims there are
many more such compilers available or soon to be available. Here is a list
mentioned in the MSDN Magazine (Sep 2000, Pg 63):
APL, CAML, Cobol, Haskell, Mercury, ML, Oberon, Oz, Pascal, Perl, Python,
Scheme, and Smalltalk. It also state that Rational is working on a .NET
compliant Java compiler.

5. It seems Jeffrey Richter believes this technology will be available on
other O/S. (After reading his articles in MSDN Sep-00 and Oct-00, I tend to
agree).

Since this subject came up I did some reading and found very interesting
information about this technology, which makes it far more interesting than
I originally anticipated.

Should anyone be interested, I can possibly post a simplified, summary
description, of this technology.

Ron

Here is the makefiles

the tutor01.bc is For FWH +BCC55
it use the tutor01 sample from the fwh samples dir

the tutor01.bc is C4W +MSVC.

Since i dont know any name of an sample application of C4W . replace the
tutor01.c and tutor01.obj with an valid one or use
hbmake tutor01.vc -e
choose the win32 option
choose MSVC as compiler
choose C4W as graphics library
input the location of the C4W root instalation dir. example c:\c4w

select the files that conponds the app

------=_NextPart_000_0009_01C066E0.EBF540C0
Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="Tutor01.bc"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable
Content-Disposition: attachment;
	filename="Tutor01.bc"

#BCC
VERSION=3DBCB01
!ifndef BCB
BCB =3D $(MAKEDIR)\..
!endif
!ifndef BHC
BHC =3D $(HMAKEDIR)\..
!endif

FWH =3D c:\fwh                                 =20
PROJECT =3D tutor01.exe
OBJFILES =3D tutor01.obj
CFILES =3D tutor01.c
RESFILES =3D=20
RESDEPEN =3D $(RESFILES)
LIBFILES =3D $(FWH)\lib\fiveh.lib $(FWH)\lib\fivec.lib lang.lib vm.lib =
rtl.lib rdd.lib macro.lib pp.lib dbfntx.lib dbfcdx.lib common.lib =
gtwin.lib
DEFFILE =3D=20
HARBOURFLAGS =3D
CFLAG1 =3D  -OS $(CFLAGS) -d -L$(BHC)\lib;$(FWH)\lib -c
CFLAG2 =3D  -I$(BHC)\include;$(BCB)\include
RFLAGS =3D=20
LFLAGS =3D -L$(BCB)\lib\obj;$(BCB)\lib;$(BHC)\lib;$(FWH)\lib -Gn -M -m =
-s-Tpe
IFLAGS =3D=20
LINKER =3D ilink32
=20
ALLOBJ =3D c0w32.obj $(OBJFILES)
ALLRES =3D $(RESFILES)
ALLLIB =3D $(LIBFILES) import32.lib cw32.lib
.autodepend
=20
#COMMANDS
.cpp.obj:
$(BCB)\BIN\bcc32 $(CFLAG1) $(CFLAG2) -o$* $*
=20
.c.obj:
$(BCB)\BIN\bcc32 -I$(BHC)\include $(CFLAG1) $(CFLAG2) -o$* $**
=20
.prg.c:
$(BHC)\bin\harbour -n -I$(BHC)\include $(HARBOURFLAGS) -I$(FWH)\include =
-o$* $**
=20
.rc.res:
$(BCB)\BIN\brcc32 $(RFLAGS) $<
=20
#BUILD
=20
$(PROJECT): $(CFILES) $(OBJFILES) $(RESDEPEN) $(DEFFILE)
    $(BCB)\BIN\$(LINKER) @&&!
    $(LFLAGS) +
    $(ALLOBJ), +
    $(PROJECT),, +
    $(ALLLIB), +
    $(DEFFILE), +
    $(ALLRES)=20
!

------=_NextPart_000_0009_01C066E0.EBF540C0
Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="tutor01.vc"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable
Content-Disposition: attachment;
	filename="tutor01.vc"

#BCC
VERSION=3DBCB01
!ifndef BCB
BCB =3D $(MAKEDIR)\..
!endif
!ifndef BHC
BHC =3D $(HMAKEDIR)\..
!endif
=20
C4W =3Dc:\c4w                                 =20
PROJECT =3D tutor01.exe
OBJFILES =3D tutor01.obj
CFILES =3D tutor01.c
RESFILES =3D=20
RESDEPEN =3D $(RESFILES)
LIBFILES =3D $(C4W)\c4wclass.lib $(C4W)\wbrowset.lib $(C4W)\otabt.lib =
$(C4W)\clip4win.liblang.lib vm.lib rtl.lib rdd.lib macro.lib pp.lib =
dbfntx.lib dbfcdx.lib common.lib gtwin.lib
DEFFILE =3D=20
HARBOURFLAGS =3D
CFLAG1 =3D  -I$(INCLUDE_DIR) -TP -W3 -nologo $(C_USR) $(CFLAGS)
CFLAG2 =3D  -c
RFLAGS =3D=20
LFLAGS =3D /LIBPATH:$(BCB)\lib;$(BHC)\lib;$(C4W)\lib /SUBSYSTEM:CONSOLE
IFLAGS =3D=20
LINKER =3D link
=20
ALLOBJ =3D $(C4W)\initc.obj$(OBJFILES)
ALLRES =3D $(RESFILES)
ALLLIB =3D $(LIBFILES) comdlg32.lib shell32.lib user32.lib gdi32.lib
=20
#COMMANDS
.cpp.obj:
$(BCB)\bin\cl $(CFLAG1) $(CFLAG2) -Fo$* $*
=20
.c.obj:
$(BCB)\bin\cl -I$(BHC)\include $(CFLAG1) $(CFLAG2) -Fo$* $**
=20
.prg.c:
$(BHC)\bin\harbour -n -I$(BHC)\include $(HARBOURFLAGS) -I$(C4W)\include =
-o$* $**
=20
.rc.res:
$(BCB)\BIN\rc $(RFLAGS) $<
=20
#BUILD

$(PROJECT): $(CFILES) $(OBJFILES) $(RESDEPEN) $(DEFFILE)
    $(BCB)\BIN\$(LINKER) @&&!
    $(LFLAGS)
    $(ALLOBJ)=20
    $(PROJECT)
    $(PROJECTMAP)
    $(ALLLIB)=20
    $(DEFFILE)=20
    $(ALLRES)=20
!

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec 15 20:37:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Fri Dec 15 20:37:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] hb_gcAll() // Garbage collector
Message-ID: <001901c06700$79ee1180$8604d2cc@san.rr.com>

We've isolated the gpf to this craziness:
If a call to fwriteline() has an alias reference in the parameter
definition, we will gpf later in hb_gcAll().
If we pull the parameter stuff into a string variable and then pass the
variable, nothing crashes.

This works:
           cstr := upper(padr(dummy->(fieldget(nid)),nLen) )
           fwriteline(nhandle, cfield + cstr + " is already in the
database." )

This blows up (later):
           fwriteline(nhandle, cfield +
upper(padr(dummy->(fieldget(nid)),nLen) ) + " is already in the database." )

Further whittling indicates that it is the "dummy->" alias that makes the
difference.
Is it possible that, while trying to set up the stack for the function call,
looking up the alias symbol corrupts something?

Brian Hays
Abacus Data Systems, Inc



From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Sun Dec 17 14:27:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Martin Vogel)

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Mon Dec 18 11:07:01 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Chen Kedem)
Date: Mon Dec 18 11:07:01 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Re: changes in sourceforge CVS ?
References: <3A3E30A0.F57@synel.co.il> <3A3E3214.DE4@synel.co.il>
Message-ID: <3A3E3594.6142@synel.co.il>

Ok, from .ssh directory I delete: known_hosts, random_seed
and then re-login:

-----------------------------------------------------------------
rem **** CVS - BEGIN ****
SET HOMEDRIVE=C:
SET HOMEPATH=\CVS
SET CVSROOT=:ext:USERNAME@cvs.Harbour-project.sourceforge.net:/cvsroot/Harbour-project
SET CVS_RSH=ssh
SET HOME=C:\CVS\
rem  **** CVS - END ****
ssh -l USERNAME Harbour-project.sourceforge.net
-----------------------------------------------------------------

(replace USERNAME with your sourceforge user name)
you'll then asked to key in your password after
that you'll get into the shell prompt, type: exit
to end this session.
after that you could work back on the CVS as before.

  Chen.

storage. mbox format, however, is very common. So, the chances are that what
you call "UNIX format" is mbox format. IOW, you've probably got exactly what
Phil is after.

For those digest users that were complaining about mime in the 
messages, there is an option to turn it off.

Go to your personal control page and set mime/plain to plain 
instead of mime.

I can reach my control page by going to:

http://www.matrixlist.com/mailman/options/harbour/midnight@the-
oasis.net

(of course, you substitute your email address instead of mine.)

You will see an option part way down the left side, 

Get MIME or Plain Text Digests? 

If you have any problems with MIME digests, select plain text.

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Thu Dec 28 18:50:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Thu Dec 28 18:50:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] array by reference memory problems
Message-ID: <000801c07129$aa4bdc30$921a5e18@bh>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0005_01C070E6.9B947280
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit


The attached test goes into an infinite internal loop if line 23 passes aTmp
by reference with @aTmp.

The same code runs fine under Clipper.

I am trying to uncover a nasty bug where, in a full-sized FWH app, an array
becomes NIL after being passed around a few layers.  I am now suspicious
that if the array variable is passed in by reference, then passed again by
reference _In A CodeBlock_, this is the problem--especially if the codeblock
has been stored in an array or object and eval'ed later.

This current test yields this hang-up, so I'm hopeful it will lead to a fix
for the original problem, which I can duplicate in a small FWH test app but
not yet in a straight Harbour applet.

The test is modeled after and simplifies  the  FWH menu scenario.  In trying
to simplify it, I have an array pretending to be the main window object (the
test currently uses no classes at all).
This array simply holds an " ON INIT" codeblock that creates the "menu",
which is also stored in the main array/object.  The "menu" is just an array
of action blocks (only one is created).

When that codeblock is eval'ed, it calls a function that receives aTmp.  If
it was set up to come in by reference, Harbour chokes.  If not, all is well.

TIA for any help on this!!

Brian

 atest3.prg

------=_NextPart_000_0005_01C070E6.9B947280
Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="atest3.prg"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable
Content-Disposition: attachment;
	filename="atest3.prg"

#include "common.ch"

function Main()

   local i, cStr, aTmp

   aTmp :=3D array(20,10)
   aTmp[1,1] :=3D 1
   aTmp[2,2] :=3D 2

   Main1(aTmp)
   ?
RETURN

FUNCTION Main1 (aTmp)
local aWinObj[2], bAction
#define A_INIT 1
#define A_MENU 2

// aWinObj[A_INIT] Contains a block that sets aWinObj[A_MENU]
// aWinObj[A_MENU] will contain an array of codeblock(s)

aWinObj[A_INIT] :=3D {|| aWinObj[A_MENU] :=3D buildmenu(aTmp, .t.) }
//  change Above to   buildmenu(@aTmp)    to blow up later


? valtype(aWinObj[A_INIT]), "should be B, this should be 1:", aTmp[1,1]
funcActivate(aWinObj)

RETURN nil


FUNCTION funcActivate (aWinObjLocal)
   ? eval(aWinObjLocal[A_INIT]), "evaled aWinObjLocal[A_INIT] to store =
block as if in a menu"
   ? valtype(aWinObjLocal[A_MENU]), "should be A, this should be 1:", =
len(aWinObjLocal[A_MENU])
   ? valtype(aWinObjLocal[A_MENU, 1]), "should be B"
   ?
   wait "press a key to simulate menu selection"
   ? eval(aWinObjLocal[A_MENU, 1]), "evaled aWinObjLocal[A_MENU] to eval =
menu action"

RETURN nil

FUNCTION buildmenu(aTmp)
local aActions[1]
aActions[1] :=3D {|| Test(@aTmp) }
? "in buildmenu"
RETURN aActions

FUNCTION Test(aTmp)
   ? "In Test", valtype(aTmp)
RETURN nil


------=_NextPart_000_0005_01C070E6.9B947280--


From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec 29 00:49:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Ron Pinkas)
Date: Fri Dec 29 00:49:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] array by reference memory problems
In-Reply-To: <000801c07129$aa4bdc30$921a5e18@bh>
Message-ID: <LOBBKAFMMFGJIKLMEPAKAEDKDIAA.ron@profit-master.com>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0000_01C07118.4EC8A520
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

Brian, Ryszard, All,

Very interesting, the infinite loop is in source/vm/itemapi.c in
hb_itemUnRef(). This can be overcome by changing the line:

            pItem = hb_codeblockGetRef( *pLocal, pItem );
with:
            pItem = *pLocal;

but... this is not the proper fix! Ryszard ?

******** IMPORTANT *********

In reviewing this I have noticed something very strange with Clipper and
Array Vars passed by reference. It seems the Clipper is buggy here, note the
following:

aVar := { 1 }
? ValType( aVar ), ValType( @aVar ) // A U

Clipper reports the type of Array passed by reference as UNDEF. Further it
seems to not retain assignment into the variable by lower level function as
it should.

Please review the attached sample for an interesting test.

FWIW Harbour appear to not display this bug, and appears to work correctly.

Ron

> The attached test goes into an infinite internal loop if line 23
> passes aTmp
> by reference with @aTmp.
>
> The same code runs fine under Clipper.
>
> I am trying to uncover a nasty bug where, in a full-sized FWH
> app, an array
> becomes NIL after being passed around a few layers.  I am now suspicious
> that if the array variable is passed in by reference, then passed again by
> reference _In A CodeBlock_, this is the problem--especially if
> the codeblock
> has been stored in an array or object and eval'ed later.
>
> This current test yields this hang-up, so I'm hopeful it will
> lead to a fix
> for the original problem, which I can duplicate in a small FWH
> test app but
> not yet in a straight Harbour applet.
>
> The test is modeled after and simplifies  the  FWH menu scenario.
>  In trying
> to simplify it, I have an array pretending to be the main window
> object (the
> test currently uses no classes at all).
> This array simply holds an " ON INIT" codeblock that creates the "menu",
> which is also stored in the main array/object.  The "menu" is
> just an array
> of action blocks (only one is created).
>
> When that codeblock is eval'ed, it calls a function that receives
> aTmp.  If
> it was set up to come in by reference, Harbour chokes.  If not,
> all is well.
>
> TIA for any help on this!!
>
> Brian

------=_NextPart_000_0000_01C07118.4EC8A520
Content-Type: application/octet-stream;
	name="VarRef.prg"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit
Content-Disposition: attachment;
	filename="VarRef.prg"

Function Main()

   LOCAL bVar, aArray := { 1 }

   ? ValType( aArray ), ValType( @aArray )

   bVar := BlockFun( @aArray )

   ? Eval( bVar )

   ? ValType( aArray ), aArray

RETURN NIL

Function BlockFun( x )

   ? "In BlockFun():", ValType( x )

RETURN { || Modify( @x ) }

Function Modify( xVar )

   ? "In Modify():", ValType( xVar )

   xVar := "Attempted Modified in Test()"

RETURN xVar

------=_NextPart_000_0000_01C07118.4EC8A520--

> Clipper reports the type of Array passed by reference as UNDEF. Further it
> seems to not retain assignment into the variable by lower level
> function as
> it should.

The above is true *only* if the lower level function is called by means of a
code block created by a lower level function.

Brian,

Here is the smallest sample I found to demonstrate this problem:

It is important to note that the problem will *not* manifest itself if
abVar[2] is set directly, as opposed to the intermediate evaluation of the
block abVar[1].

// ---- aVarRef.prg ---- //
Function Main()

   LOCAL abVar[2], aArray := { 1 }

   abVar[1] := {|| abVar[2] := BlockFun( @aArray ) }

   Eval( abVar[1] )

   ? Eval( abVar[2] )

   ? ValType( aArray ), aArray

RETURN NIL

Function BlockFun( x )

   ? "In BlockFun():", ValType( x )

RETURN {|| x := "Modified" }
// ---- aVarRef.prg ---- //

Ron

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec 29 06:01:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Ron Pinkas)
Date: Fri Dec 29 06:01:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] array by reference (Ryszard)
In-Reply-To: <001f01c07177$003f76e0$921a5e18@bh>
Message-ID: <LOBBKAFMMFGJIKLMEPAKAEEADIAA.ron@profit-master.com>

Ryszard,

I found some very strange problems, it appears that the following sample
will create Cyclic References which causes the Infinite Loop in
hb_itemUnRef().

// -------------------------------------------------------------------------
-- //
Function Main()

   #DEFINE ERROR // comment this line will hide this problem.

   #ifdef ERROR
      LOCAL abVar[2], aArray := { 1 }
   #else
      PRIVATE abVar[2], aArray := { 1 }
   #endif

   abVar[1] := {|| abVar[2] := BlockFun( @aArray ) }

   ? abVar[1]
   Eval( abVar[1] )
   //WAIT // Uncomment to see stranger issue.

   ? abVar[2]
   ? Eval( abVar[2] )
   //WAIT // Uncomment to see stranger issue.

   ? ValType( aArray ), aArray

RETURN NIL

Function BlockFun( x )

   ? "In BlockFun():", ValType( x )

RETURN {|| x := "Modified" }
// -------------------------------------------------------------------------
-- //

If we use PRIVATE instead of LOCAL the problem disappears!

If you uncomment the WAIT lines in the sample PRG, it does some real strange
stuff.

I have added Cyclic Detection to hb_itemUnRef() as follows to show the
problem:

PHB_ITEM hb_itemUnRef( PHB_ITEM pItem )
{
   int iBaseItems = 0, i;
   BOOL bCyclic = FALSE;
   PHB_ITEM pBaseItem, *pBaseItems = NULL;

   HB_TRACE(HB_TR_DEBUG, ("hb_itemUnRef(%p)", pItem));

   while( HB_IS_BYREF( pItem ) )
   {
      printf( "%i Type: %i\n", pItem, pItem->type );

      if( HB_IS_MEMVAR( pItem ) )
      {
         HB_VALUE_PTR pValue;

         pValue = *( pItem->item.asMemvar.itemsbase ) +
pItem->item.asMemvar.offset +
                     pItem->item.asMemvar.value;
         pBaseItem = &pValue->item;
      }
      else
      {
         if( pItem->item.asRefer.value >= 0 )
         {
            if( pItem->item.asRefer.offset == 0 )
            {
               /* a reference to a static variable */
               pBaseItem = *( pItem->item.asRefer.BasePtr.itemsbase ) +
pItem->item.asRefer.value;
            }
            else
            {
               /* a reference to a local variable */
               HB_ITEM_PTR *pLocal;
               pLocal = *( pItem->item.asRefer.BasePtr.itemsbasePtr ) +
pItem->item.asRefer.offset + pItem->item.asRefer.value;
               pBaseItem = *pLocal;
            }
         }
         else
         {
            /* local variable referenced in a codeblock
            */
            HB_ITEM_PTR *pLocal;
            pLocal = *( pItem->item.asRefer.BasePtr.itemsbasePtr ) +
pItem->item.asRefer.offset;
            pBaseItem = hb_codeblockGetRef( *pLocal, pItem );
         }
      }

      for( i = 0; i < iBaseItems; i++ )
      {
         pItem = pBaseItems[i];
         if( pItem == pBaseItem )
         {
            bCyclic = TRUE;
         }
      }

      if( bCyclic )
      {
         printf( "Cyclic\n" );
         break;
      }
      else
      {
         iBaseItems++;
         if( pBaseItems == NULL )
         {
            pBaseItems = (PHB_ITEM *) hb_xalloc( sizeof( PHB_ITEM ) );
         }
         else
         {
            pBaseItems = (PHB_ITEM *) hb_xrealloc( pBaseItems,
izeof( PHB_ITEM ) * iBaseItems );
         }
         pBaseItems[ iBaseItems - 1 ] = pBaseItem;
         pItem = pBaseItem;
      }
   }

   if( pBaseItems )
   {
      hb_xfree( pBaseItems );
   }

   printf( "Returned: %i\n", pItem );

   return pItem;
}

Ron

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec 29 13:49:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Fri Dec 29 13:49:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] CHANGELOG: 2000-12-29 01:30 UTC-0800
References: <000701c0717a$d6dc6250$921a5e18@bh> <20001229095405.O15915@hagbard.davep.org>
Message-ID: <001b01c071c8$ae2c7180$921a5e18@bh>

Dave:
>>Doesn't the function I mentioned before provide just such an abstraction?

Not really.  HB_OSNEWLINE is a PRG-level function that returns a pointer to
a static buffer from console.c.  I didn't realize at first that a similar
C-level call was just above it (hb_conNewLine).  But console.c itself just
does
#if defined(OS_UNIX_COMPATIBLE)
   #define CRLF_BUFFER_LEN 2
#else
   #define CRLF_BUFFER_LEN 3
#endif
...to set this up.

What memoline needs is the constant CRLF_BUFFER_LEN, and it didn't seem
right to get the string pointer then get the length of the string every
time.
Can we move this constant to hbsetup.h?
I would propose creating one there called OS_EOL_LEN, and have console.c use
   #define CRLF_BUFFER_LEN   OS_EOL_LEN + 1

Brian


From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Fri Dec 29 14:57:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (David G. Holm)
Date: Fri Dec 29 14:57:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] Accesing CVS

References: <NCBBJKNMIDPJNLJCHCHIEEMCFLAA.harbour@winfakt.com>

** Reply to message from "Antonio Linares" <alinares@fivetech.com> on
Fri, 29 Dec 2000 08:26:47 +0100

> But what to do ??? :-)
> 
> Why is that hapening ?

Because SourceForge changed their hardware, as was reported in a direct
email from SourceForge to all project managers that someone even copied
to this very list. What you need to do is go to your .ssh directory,
delete the known_hosts and random_seed files, then run 'ssh -l <cUserID>
cvs.Harbour-project.sourceforge.net' and enter your SourceForge password
when prompted.

HI Dave,

I think it could be good idea to pack harbour.spec into harbour directory at
harbour-*.tar.gz file. In such way everyone who take archive will be able to
make rpms (src and bin) with one command:
rpm -ta harbour-*.tar.gz

After that you can remove harbour-*.src.rpm files from harbour download
page eliminating rpm compatibility problem (eg. RPM4 src files cannot be
rebuild on system with earlier RPM version without some additional work)

regards,
Przemek

From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Sat Dec 30 13:55:03 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Sat Dec 30 13:55:03 2000
Subject: [Harbour] CHANGELOG: 2000-12-29 01:30 UTC-0800
References: <200012291959.eBTJxC222703@thor.parrett.net>
Message-ID: <002501c07292$b99deba0$921a5e18@bh>

David:

> > Added OS_UNIX_COMPATIBLE test for single-byte EOL markers
>
> Why not use hb_conNewLine()?

Here's my response to Dave. Let me know if you like my proposal:

.....  I didn't realize at first that a similar C-level call was just above
it (hb_conNewLine).  But console.c itself just
does
#if defined(OS_UNIX_COMPATIBLE)
   #define CRLF_BUFFER_LEN 2
#else
   #define CRLF_BUFFER_LEN 3
#endif
...to set this up.

What memoline needs is the constant CRLF_BUFFER_LEN, and it didn't seem
right to get the string pointer then get the length of the string every
time.
Can we move this constant to hbsetup.h?
I would propose creating one there called OS_EOL_LEN, and have console.c use
   #define CRLF_BUFFER_LEN   OS_EOL_LEN + 1

Brian


From harbour@lists.harbour-project.org  Sat Dec 30 14:44:02 2000
From: harbour@lists.harbour-project.org (Brian Hays)
Date: Sat Dec 30 14:44:02 2000
Subject: [Harbour] RDD - SET OPTIMIZE
Message-ID: <000b01c07299$88e22a60$921a5e18@bh>

The clipper NG implies SET OPTIMIZE is specific to a workarea, but I don't
believe this is the case.
I've never used it (always used explicit cmx* or cm* functions).  Does
anyone know for sure if this is a normal global setting?

There's a new setting that we should add that is equivalent to the Clipmore
cmDoLinear() -- whether or not to immediately resolve partially-  or
non-optimized filters (this can take a lot of time when the SET FILTER is
executed).  The alternative is to dynamically resolve records as you move
through the database.

Should we add a new SET OPT_RESOLVE_IMMEDIATE ON/OFF to set()?

I need to add support for these to RDDADS, but since they also apply to
dbfcdx I would rather do it through the RDD...

P.S.
I believe Ryszard suggested once that we add an extension to optionally make
SET DELETED specific to a workarea; if so we should do this for SET OPTIMIZE
too.

Brian Hays

Sorry - I'm very late responding. :-(

"1. I am not an MS advocate."

I definitely wasn't meaning in any way to suggest you were (or were
not).

"2. The "Language Independent" was quoted and astericized exactly because=
 I
don't necessarily agree with the description."

I rather thought so.

"3. .NET It is pushed by MS as a Language Independent technology, because=

from the architecture stand point, it is indeed language and even CPU
independent."

It's certainly pushed that way.  COM/OLE/DCOM/ActiveX have also been
pushed like that but have not exactly amounted to much.  NT was also
pushed somewhat similarly but then the other supported CPUs were
dropped.  IOW, MS have a less than good track record.  (You probably
know this. <g>)  I'm not even going to mention other bandwagons MS
have joined then abandoned. <BG>

My main comment was meant to apply especially to the part about MFC.
For many (most?) of the things MFC is used for, the CLR appears to be
[searches for words] irrelevant/neutral.  For most things, the CLR
doesn't look like a replacement for MFC, does it?

Happy New Year (to Everyone, not only Ron :-),
